Free Talk

A Word of Wisdom

— Long

Love in this world is not the exclusive privilege of married couples, just as being a married couple does not necessarily mean having love.

As long as terms like "prostitute" and "concubine" are not abolished, the mantra of gender equality cannot be truly proclaimed.

Life is like a riddle. If a prophet were to reveal everything, what interest would there be? Therefore, there are no true prophets in the world, nor will a prophet ever succeed.

A woman around the age of twenty can be considered the most adored by men. Therefore, during this period, a woman should carefully use her discerning eyes to choose a member of the opposite sex who values both affection and righteousness as a lifelong partner.

In the arena of love, men find a woman's desire to buy clothes the most daunting thing, while women find a man's proposal of marriage the most difficult to handle.

The most embarrassing moment for someone who likes to boast is when they are exposed.

The rise and fall of the nation is the responsibility of every citizen. If we can use one less foreign product, we will have fulfilled one more fraction of our responsibility to save the country.

Those who are ugly in appearance all know the art of adornment, while those who are morally depraved rarely know how to correct their ways. Therefore, the number of hypocritical people increases daily, while the number of honest people decreases daily.

Most young men and women can only see beauty and money, and lack the ability to examine talent and virtue. Therefore, happy marriages and healthy families are not common in society.

A Record of a Ford Airplane Test Ride

— Cheng Zhizheng

This Ford airplane, coming from America via Europe and Russia to our country, has been warmly welcomed in Shenyang and Tianjin. With its soaring flight, the people of Shanghai have been paying attention to it. The plane also offered test flights to various sectors. The day before the opening of the Industry and Commerce Conference, the plane was specially arranged to carry a portion of the members to Beijing. Mr. Zhong Weicheng, President of the Jiaotong University Railway Management College in this city, was also one of the experts invited. He flew on the plane that day. Now that the Industry and Commerce Conference has come to a close and President Zhong has returned to Shanghai, the reporter visited him and he shared detailed information about his experience on the test flight. Here is a record of some of it to inform those who are concerned about air transport.

Appearance of the Plane The Ford airplane is larger than the ones used by the Shanghai-Chengdu Aviation. The Shanghai-Chengdu planes can only carry seven passengers, while this plane can carry up to sixteen. Furthermore, ordinary planes have only one engine, while the Ford has a large engine in the middle and one on each side. This setup not only increases the speed but also prevents the entire flight from being affected by the damage of one engine. The entire fuselage is made of metal and is extremely strong and beautiful. The wings are several feet long, and the fuselage is painted with various promotional designs.

Pre-flight Inspection One hour before the flight, a pilot comes to inspect whether the internal components are complete. After this inspection, one can feel more at ease, as any questions about the components will lead to the flight being suspended for repairs, rather than a rash departure.

The plane circles the field once and then soars into the wind.

What can be seen in the plane The seats in the plane are very spacious, divided into two rows with seven seats in each row. The seats are all backrest sofas, which are exceptionally comfortable. The windows are tightly closed, but one can still look out and overlook the earth. One can see a green field, the Yangtze River like a ribbon, and the railways like curved ink lines. Other people, animals, and livestock cannot be seen with the naked eye.

Giving out Cotton Wool Those who are experienced with aviation must carry cotton wool when flying. This is because the air pressure at high altitudes is lower. When descending from high altitudes, if cotton wool is not placed in the ears, the eardrums can be easily damaged by the excessively high air pressure in the lower regions. That day, President Zhong and others did not bring this item, so those experienced in this matter gave it to everyone on the spot, who regarded it as a precious gift. However, the plane flew very low that day, so even without this item, there would have been no major problems. The most interesting thing is that the sound of the engine is like thunder during the flight, so even those sitting next to each other cannot talk to each other, but can only make gestures with their hands.

Torrential Rain When arriving in Beijing and descending, the rain was pouring down, but people sitting on the plane did not feel it at first. After getting off the plane, the company used cars to transport the members to their residences, which was very thoughtful. Looking at the time, it took only one hour and twenty minutes on the way. Compared to the train, even an express train takes more than eight hours. How convenient it is!

Like Sitting in a Car Mr. Zhong also said that riding on an airplane is as comfortable as riding in a car. However, cars sometimes have bumps due to uneven roads, while airplanes are incomparably stable and absolutely safe. In the future, this industry will definitely have significant advancements, which can be said with certainty.

The Right in the Air According to the host of the Ford company, Mr. Ford himself is already a car king. He has recently invested tens of millions to focus on aviation and has his son manage it. His intention is to have his son be an air king. It is said that there will surely be accomplished people after those with great virtue, and one who follows in their father's footsteps is worthy of admiration.

Anticipation in Beijing Hundreds of people in Beijing have signed up to try out the plane, which shows that the people of our country have a considerable interest in it. However, the plane will only be available for people in Beijing to try after President Chiang comes to Shanghai to test it out and fly to Beijing. In short, Ford's visit this time has a great impact on air transport in our country.

Medical Palace Anecdotes

— Jing Mengdie

During the Double Ninth Festival, while traveling in Changzhou, two or three close friends visited me. Lighting a lamp for a late-night conversation, one of the guests, who had just returned from Shanghai, told a recent story from the medical community. The story was extremely tragic yet also extremely amusing. I record it with my brush to reveal a glimpse of the darkness in the medical world and the dangers that those seeking passage through the maze of the sea face.

In the bustling Shanghai, countless people from Ningbo have become wealthy through business. A certain young man, the son of a wealthy merchant from Ningbo, was handsome and enjoyed a flamboyant lifestyle, frequently frolicking in brothels for pleasure. Extreme pleasure leads to sorrow, and he contracted a venereal disease, which is common. He secretly told his friend about his illness, and the friend, who had some medical knowledge, said that it was just a chancre, caused by uncleanliness, and not true syphilis. If treated early, the disease would be easily cured. However, the young man had grown up in a wealthy family, was accustomed to extravagance, and considered the disease to be in a critical area. He would spare no expense to cure it and aimed for a quick recovery to resume his former pleasures. He immediately sought treatment at a famous and expensive hospital. The doctor in the hospital asked him to undress and briefly examined him, nodding slightly, saying he knew. He then led the young man into a secret room, ordered him to lie on a couch, and administered anesthesia. The young man was unconscious for a while, and when he woke up, he saw heavy bandages below. He felt something was wrong and reached out to touch it, but the doctor warned him not to move rashly, as he had just undergone surgery. The young man's heart was still not at ease. That night, while lying in the hospital, he secretly reached into the blankets and carefully felt it with his hand, and was shocked and fainted. The thing between his legs was completely gone, having been castrated. The bird, the bird was gone, without wings, and placed in a glass bottle as an exhibit. Grieving intensely, he couldn't help but cry, but the attendant quickly stopped him, saying that it was not allowed by the hospital rules. When he recovered from his illness, he negotiated with the hospital, but the affairs officer angrily said, "Who told you to contract this disease? Keeping your life intact is already a virtue. Why do you complain?" The young man ultimately failed due to lack of power and gave up. However, he was the only son and had no descendants. His resentment can be imagined. Did the doctor recklessly perform castration as a form of surgery, intending to punish him for promiscuity? Is this any different from seizing a person's cow because it trespassed on their field? Isn't this technique extremely frightening?

Record of the Star Late-Night Banquet

— Xu Xiaoting

Because Yanqiu, Shaolou, and others from the singing and opera troupe attached to the Star Film Company will soon be completing their contracts after coming from the south to perform, President Zhou Jianyun hosted a banquet at the company last night at one o'clock as a farewell dinner. He invited many guests to join as companions. Those who attended included Shaoqing, Huogong, Sheyu, Lü Gongzi, Bao, and your humble brother. From the opera world, there were Mr. and Mrs. Zhu Naigen, Mr. Luo Liangsheng, and Mr. Wang Shiyong (the owner of Chunfeng Hall). Even Mr. Chen Yanheng, who rarely socializes, graciously attended. From the acting world, there were Yanqiu, Shaolou, Miaoxiang, Ruian, and Tongsheng Wujie, along with the company's film stars, such as Zhengqiu, Yuanlong, Xiaoqiu, Tang Jie, Zhan Fei, and the playwright Hong Shen, creating a grand gathering. Yanqiu, Shaolou, and Miaoxiang arrived at the banquet from the Yage Collection at two o'clock. The host arranged for them to be seated. Zheng Jun and Xiaoqiu, who were sitting at the same table, were quite skilled at drumming and playing the qin. Now, seeing Mr. Chen Yanheng, Yanqiu, and Shaolou in attendance, they could not miss this opportunity to enjoy their wonderful performances. They incited President Jianyun to turn to Mr. Yanheng for assistance, and everyone echoed their support. Mr. Yanheng smiled and agreed, much to Xiaoqiu's delight. Tongshan played the drums while Yanqiu sang a section from "Fen River Bend" and Shaolou sang a section from "Zhuangyuan Pu." One was a unique expression of new tunes, while the other followed the styles of Uncle Yan, each with their own merits. By then, the clock struck four, and the guests began to bid farewell. There are four things about this banquet that must be highlighted: (1) Zhengqiu, Yanqiu, Shaolou, Tongshan, and Mr. Yanheng were at the same table and discussed the merits of new and old operas and films. Even those sitting far away were captivated. (2) Shaoqing and Miaoxiang were seated next to each other. The two gentlemen were of similar stature and had similar faces (especially the areas above the nose and teeth were most alike, although Shaoqing's mouth was slightly wider than Miaoxiang's). Those sitting at the same table could not help but carefully observe their expressions and tones to see if they were the same. (3) Yanqiu and Shaolou were attending the Yage Collection banquet. Jianyun was afraid that they would be late, so he specially asked Huogong to accompany them and urge them on. Yanqiu sings well as the female lead in "Qijie" [The Escort], and Shaolou is also good as the male lead in "Qijie" (Qin [Zhongyu] Dispatch). Those at the same table jokingly called Huogong a兼職jiecha, or part-time escort. (4) Shaolou and Xiaoqiu are both in their twenties, handsome and lively, and both rich in artistic talent. Now that they are working hard in old operas and films, the future is long. They will definitely be able to add a unique color to the art world in our country, so it seems appropriate to congratulate the two gentlemen in advance with this banquet.

A Note on the "Jazz Singer" Tie

— Zhou Lang

Within the past month, a new type of Western-style tie has become popular in Shanghai. This tie is produced by a company in New York and London and is specially designed for the promotion of the film "The Jazz Singer," released this year by the Warner Brothers film company. The colors are quite vibrant, and the quality is also high, with various musical notes and symbols woven into it to represent the film's title. Because of its artistic appeal, the general public is vying to purchase it, and it has become a trend in New York. When the film premiered at the largest theater in the area, the Roxy, sales were even stronger. It is said that they are also being sold in Shanghai when the film premieres at the Nanjing Theater, but the price is extremely high, around four yuan each. They are being sold through the Wing On Company. It is said that the film has many new advertising methods, and the tie advertisement is one of them. Others, such as aerial advertisements and cigarette advertisements, are also new, unique, and eye-catching, truly the latest advertising techniques.

News from the art world The famous painter and calligrapher Yu Jianhua will hold a personal exhibition on the fourth floor of the Ningbo Tongxiang Association on Xizang Road for three days, from the 15th to the 17th of this month. On the 9th, at noon, he hosted a banquet at the Xinghua Lou, inviting famous figures from Shanghai, painters and calligraphers, and journalists. At the same time, he held a preview of a portion of his works. The works were dazzling and beautiful, and guests were vying to reserve them. A total of one hundred pieces have been produced, and more than seventy pieces have already been reserved. I have also reserved a "Viewing Waterfalls in the Shade of Pines," which is imitated from Shitao. His brushwork is smooth and refined and does not fall into the commonplace. It is truly a masterpiece. It is said that there are still reservation tickets available for sale at the Hezhong Company at the intersection of Wuma Road and Qipan Street. (Juan)

A Short Note on the San Francisco Chinatown (Part 1)

— Kang Kang

San Francisco is the transliteration of San Francisco. The Japanese call it Sang Kong, the Cantonese call it Big Port or, based on the name Golden Gate, Jinmen (Golden Gate). The language of [通欲 unclear] also calls it Old Jinshan (Old Gold Mountain). In fact, they are all the same place. Calling it Big Port is because the most overseas Chinese are here and it has the largest commerce, and Sacramento, the capital of California, is second, called Second Port. Calling it Old Jinshan is because in the early years, most of the overseas Chinese came for gold digging, so it was called Jinshan (Gold Mountain). Later, Nevada had gold mines and more overseas Chinese, so it was called New Jinshan, and this place was called Old Jinshan.

The Chinatown occupies about one-tenth of the city's area, near the commercial center and not far from the wharf, and is one of the earliest developed parts of the city. The current city population is about 750,000, and the number of overseas Chinese is less than 30,000, most of whom reside in Chinatown. It is about five or six streets wide and long, with trams running in the four directions. There are many narrow lanes on the left and right sides of the main streets, like Beijing's hutongs and Shanghai's longtang. It is said that before the earthquake in 1906, the roads were narrow and the houses were low, and the doors and walls were not uniform. After the reconstruction, it was slightly more organized. Generally, there are buildings of three or four floors. Except for the largest stores, the front is often a shop and the family lives in the back, as is the case in the interior. The upper two floors are apartments for rent, each with its own entrance. The municipal government of the Hong Kong and Shanghai concessions has strict regulations on building hygiene, and the circulation of sunlight and air, as well as the supply of water, fire, coal, and electricity, are all convenient.

The major stores in Chinatown are mostly on Grant Avenue, formerly known as Dupont Street. Antique art shops include Sheng Fa, Sheng Chang, Nanjing, and Beijing companies. Hotels include Shanghai Building, Republic Building, and Daguan Building. Restaurants include Xinghua Lou, Far East Lou, and Yihe Yuan. Theaters include Da Zhonghua and Da Wutai. In addition, there are grocery stores, gold and jewelry stores, fish markets, meat markets, fruit markets, and vegetable markets, all gathered here. There are also specially set up post office branches, telegraph office branches, and telephone office branches. Branches such as the Bank of East Asia and transportation companies are all managed by overseas Chinese.

European Travel Correspondence (85)

— Liu Haisu

Pilgrimage to Italy Diary

Rome, March 10, Day 8

Day Two - Colosseum - Arch of Constantine - Baths of Caracalla - Underground Church

After seeing the Arch of Constantine, I proposed:

"Let's go out of the city and see the underground catacombs first."

Everyone agreed, so we took a carriage and headed straight for Via Appia, out of the Porto Capina. Not far away was a large park dotted with palm trees and cypresses. Suddenly, it was quiet, with no cars, horses, or people. From the shade of the trees, we could see seven or eight young men and women gathered on the green lawn talking. There were no gray, square, or black houses. The horse walked in front, as if going up a mountain road, turning left and walking along the earthen mound on a dirt road. The flying gray dirt made the sweltering heat even more apparent. The heat was truly sweltering, making us dizzy. However, the archaeological temperament hidden in our hearts made us only have endless hope for the magical beauty of the ancients. Before long, the carriage stopped by the roadside on top of an earthen mound. A red and obvious ruin like a beehive stood, as silent as a devil's cave. We happily walked in, stroking the desolate remains under the dome and on the stone pillars, our bodies filled with a dismal divinity. Ah, this is the remains of the Baths of Caracalla, built in 217 AD.

Strange, truly strange. More than 1,700 years ago, Rome produced a strange emperor. If you want to add flattering words, he was a talented and creative emperor. If you want to scold him, he was a proud and extravagant tyrant. When he was happy, he built such a large building. No one can truly know why, and everyone can only say that this kind of expansive architecture was built because of Caracalla's extraordinarily extravagant ignorance. This bathhouse is extremely large, and although it is only a remaining ruin, one can still feel its overall spiritual power. From the parallel arched doors, the exquisitely carved stone pillars, and the remains, one can imagine the scene of 1,600 people bathing together. It is said that the layout of the golden house was precise, with the bathhouse in the center, exercise rooms on both sides, then competition grounds, and also libraries, dining rooms, and bedrooms. The building was 240 feet deep and 120 feet wide. Such a scale for a bathhouse is an unreasonable excess and luxury in ordinary life, but it can also serve as a symbol and memorial of Rome.

No Improvement in Yarn, Cotton, and Silk Markets

The yarn market is still weak. In fact, the sales of spot yarn are not strong, and the agents are very slack, resulting in a thicker bottom cargo. According to Japanese merchants' investigations, there are about 170,000 to 180,000 bales. With this huge amount of hoarding, the pressure on the market is increasing. Japanese merchants are hedging heavily in the distant months, and some manufacturers are taking a negative attitude and liquidating 2,000 to 3,000 bales of long positions. New lows were discovered in the previous market. At the close, Rongxinghao bought 1,700 bales in the current month, which was also entrusted by the manufacturer, and the market atmosphere slightly improved. In short, the bottom cargo is too thick, sales are not improving, and the future is still difficult to stabilize.

The man-made fiber market is shaky. The opening price of man-made fiber in the previous market rose due to the rebound of American cotton, and the market sentiment was slightly tighter, rising by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan. In the second and third 盘, a certain factory liquidated long positions, and the market sentiment suddenly loosened, with each month falling by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. In the afternoon, some long positions were bought in, rising slightly by 0.2 to 0.4 yuan. The total transaction volume for the day was 19,550 bales. It was found that Daji bought 1,050 bales, Dafeng 1,000 bales, Senkang 1,100 bales, Yuantai 1,250 bales, Gongtai 900 bales, and the rest 300 to 500 bales. Grain and River Lower Rice Prices Hover

Yesterday, more than 30 domestic boats arrived at Zhabei, and sales were still acceptable. The situation of the new japonica rice varied because the concepts of buying and selling were different. Those who were greedy for entering the market were willing to loosen the price, and those who needed to sell urgently had to slightly lower the price. Therefore, the same goods had varying market prices with a difference of 0.1 to 0.5 yuan. The general trend has turned to a fixed high price. The current inventory of local shops is insufficient because they are bearish on the market. Therefore, the japonica rice market will turn into a hovering state in the future. The aroma of the Xian rice is relatively refreshing, and the goods are sold by customers, and the large market has risen slightly. The special grade is opened at 13 yuan. Although the Du rice is also tight and popular, the entry volume of each gang is limited, and the price is slightly firm, and the high opening is 13.35 yuan. The local rice is scarce and the transaction is flat, and the market is stable and rising by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan. The sale is mainly at high prices, and both the wine stomach and the rice stomach are selective in purchasing, with the top opening at 15.85 yuan.

Yesterday, more than 20 boats arrived in Shanghai South. The trend of each gang in the main street was different. The white japonica rice of Changzhou, Wuxi, Suzhou, and other places was initially shouted up due to the soaring influence of the North Market the day before yesterday, but the sales were not expanded, and the market presented mutual rejection. However, the price of the goods opened was determined by the means of buying and selling, with an increase or decrease of 0.2 yuan. The top grade here was about 15.1 yuan, and the Suzhou gang's high-grade goods also required about 14 yuan. The early and late rice of each place on the left and south roads also continued to arrive. Since the continuous decline, the goods merchants have become a major relationship and have turned to wait and see. Therefore, the top-grade goods are slightly firm, and the medium and second grade have turned to stability. The selling path of the Xian rice is tight for customer sales and stable for shop sales. The situation is about to rise. The afternoon has already mentioned the 0.1 yuan rise. The market is currently guarding the original market due to strong sales and stagnant sentiment.

Yesterday, the Xian rice was still silent. Although sporadic small tickets continued to arrive, the sale was very dull. Therefore, recent transactions are less, the market trend is flat, and the distant future depends on how the factory will behave before there is an increase or decrease. Local News

Yesterday Was the Birthday of the Premier, All Sectors of the City Celebrated Enthusiastically

Yesterday was the 65th Anniversary of the Birthday of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, Premier of the Chinese Kuomintang. The Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department specially convened representatives from all agencies, organizations, schools, and party departments at all levels in the city, four representatives from each, to hold a memorial meeting at 9:00 am at the Republican Theater on Minguo Road in the South City. More than a thousand representatives from all sectors attended. The meeting was presided over by the Minister of Propaganda of the Municipal Party Committee, who led the attendees in a ceremony in accordance with etiquette, and then reported on the significance of the Premier's birth and the necessary understanding and efforts. After the report, representatives from the Municipal Party Department, Wu Bokang, representatives from the Municipal Government, Chen Kecheng, representatives from the Overseas Chinese Affairs Association, Xu Jigong, and others spoke in succession. Then, slogans were shouted and music was played to conclude the meeting. In the afternoon, a recreational gathering was held at the Municipal General Chamber of Commerce. In addition, all agencies, organizations, schools, and rural areas such as Jiangwan, Wusong, Pudong, Zhenru, and Meilong held separate memorial services. The details of each event are recorded as follows:

Memorial Meeting

Attending Organizations

The Municipal Government and its bureaus, Shanghai Local Court, Special District Local Court, Shanghai High Court Second Branch, Ministry of Transportation Postal Administration, Ministry of Industry and Commerce Industrial and Commercial Visiting Bureau, Central Bank, Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office, Jiangsu and Zhejiang Fisheries Affairs Bureau, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Municipal Women's Association, Municipal General Chamber of Commerce, schools, labor unions, organizations, district party departments, district branches, and other representatives, more than a thousand people.

Convention Staff

Chairman: Yang Qingyuan

Recorder: Chen Boxiu, Zhou Hanmei

Master of Ceremonies: Li Zheng

Reception: Yang Peiwen, Luo Changmin, Chen Yunhuang, Li Bingjun, Zhang Hongwei

Secretaries: Xu Xiyu, Fan Shuxiu, Ding Ruochuan, Tao Yuchuan

Chairman's Report

Fellow Representatives, Fellow Comrades, today is the 65th anniversary of the Prime Minister's birth. In 1766, the Prime Minister was born in Cuiheng Village, Xiangshan County, Guangdong. For the sixty years that followed, he devoted himself entirely to saving China and the world. (Omission) There are many great aspects of the Prime Minister's life. Now, I would like to discuss two points with you. First, the Three Principles of the People, invented by the Prime Minister. As we know, the Three Principles of the People encompass nationalism, democracy, and people's livelihood. Nationalism not only seeks freedom and equality for one's own nation but also strives for the freedom and equality of all small and weak nations in the world. Therefore, the goal of nationalism is to save international freedom and equality. After the implementation of democracy, the people have political power, including the rights to elect, recall, initiate, and referendum. Except for warlords, corrupt officials, reactionaries, and the like, all are entitled to participate in political power. It is evident that democracy seeks political freedom and equality. The Principle of People's Livelihood is divided into two aspects: equalization of land ownership and regulation of capital. The Prime Minister believed that China's objective environment was suitable for this approach and that, starting from these two methods, the goal of abolishing private property could gradually be achieved. The outline of the Three Principles of the People is so, and its greatness and profoundness are already evident. However, some idle people and scholars are arrogant and give speeches everywhere, but their arguments are not worthy of understanding the Prime Minister's Three Principles of the People and have become meaningless. Their so-called nationalism is simply to resist foreign powers and eliminate internal traitors, that is, nationalism, and at best, it is nothing more than imperialism. Can China embark on this path that others have already taken wrongly? I think you representatives understand very well, and I don't need to talk about it much. Apart from this small group of nationalists, there are also the so-called Chinese Communist bandits. The error of communism itself has been clearly refuted by the Prime Minister. However, the general Chinese Communist bandits, subsidized by Soviet rubles, act lawlessly and wreak havoc in our country's rural areas, killing, arsoning, and doing everything. They simply don't deserve to be called any ideology or revolution; they are just a bunch of local bullies, hooligans, and bandits. Therefore, China's political way out lies only in believing in the Three Principles of the People, implementing the Three Principles of the People, and realizing a new society of the people, by the people, and for the people. Second, commemorating the Prime Minister's forty years of revolutionary spirit. Since the age of twenty, the Prime Minister has strived for revolution, suffered for revolution, and gone into exile countless times. He initiated uprisings and failed countless times. Did the Prime Minister lose heart? Not only did the Prime Minister not lose heart, but he also mustered courage to work hard and struggle. His spirit of forty years as one day is so worthy of our belief and admiration. However, nowadays, the general public and comrades often become negative at the slightest setback and even more disheartened at the slightest disappointment. This kind of weak will and lack of patience is a manifestation of a shallow understanding of the revolution. Today, Nanjing is holding the Fourth Plenary Session, and all construction policies are waiting to be determined and implemented. I hope that all representatives and comrades will deeply recognize their past weaknesses, strive hard, take the Prime Minister's doctrine as the center of my thoughts, and encourage ourselves to move forward with the Prime Minister's spirit of struggle. Then, today, our commemoration of the Prime Minister's birthday will not let the Prime Minister's birthday down. The report is finished.

Convention Proposals

(1) Send a telegram of congratulations to the opening of the Fourth Plenary Session.

(2) Send a telegram requesting the Fourth Plenary Session to order the two Commanders-in-Chief, Chiang and Zhang, to eliminate the remaining warlords.

(3) Send a telegram requesting the Fourth Plenary Session to order the garrison troops in various places to eliminate bandits and communists.

(4) The Dutch government in Nanyang unreasonably oppresses our overseas Chinese. Send a telegram requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to protest seriously.

(5) The Sino-Dutch treaty has expired. Send a telegram requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to announce its abolition immediately.

Convention Slogans

1. Celebrate the Prime Minister's birthday.

2. Commemorate the Prime Minister's great spirit.

3. Strive for reform and construction.

4. Fulfill the Prime Minister's will.

5. Wipe out the Chinese Communist bandits.

6. Eradicate the reactionary remnants.

7. Severely punish the Yan-Feng warlords.

8. Down with imperialism.

9. Abolish all unequal treaties.

10. Strive for the revolutionary construction of the Three Principles of the People.

11. Complete the National Revolution.

12. Promote world harmony.

13. Support the National Government.

14. The Prime Minister's spirit never dies.

15. Long live the Kuomintang of China.

16. Long live the Republic of China.

After the ceremony, Chairman Fu Ruiwu reported on the Prime Minister's revolutionary spirit and the significance of the commemoration. Speakers included Zeng Shengdian and Fu Xiteng, who spoke on the significance of commemorating the Prime Minister's birthday and the future efforts of the Party. More than 200 people were present, including party members from various branches and representatives from all walks of life. Shanghai County All Circles

Yesterday morning at 10 a.m., all circles under the jurisdiction of Shanghai County held a Prime Minister's Birthday Commemoration Celebration Meeting at the Minhang Public Sports Field. Present were Tao Yishan, Wang Liping, Jiang Yanchou, Lu Zhe, and Han Rongling, members of the Shanghai County Party Affairs Reorganization Committee, as well as all staff members and representatives from various county-level organizations, including Ye Dedi, Fu Dianying, Cheng Keshi, Ding Guangzeng, Shi Yangyong, Li Tongrui, Cai Zhongji, Wu Jingqing, Yu Chuzhai, and Pan Jingyue. Participating groups included the Minhang Chamber of Commerce, Rural Teachers' College, Central Elementary School, Orphanage, Zhuanqiao Elementary School, etc., totaling approximately three to four thousand people. The presidium consisted of Tao Yishan, Jiang Yanchou (County Party Affairs Reorganization Committee), Ye Dezhen (County Government), Shi Yangyong (Propaganda Committee), and Wu Jingqing (Representative of All Circles in Minhang). After the ceremony, Tao Yishan of the presidium reported, roughly stating that today, sixty-four years ago, was the day Sun Yat-sen was born in Cuiheng Village, Xiangshan County, Guangdong. With the birth of the Prime Minister, the Republic of China was born, which also influenced the revolutionary spirit of all small and weak nations in the world. Our commemoration of the Prime Minister is not only a formal celebration, but also requires us to work hard according to the Prime Minister's teachings. The reactionary forces of the two rebels, Yan and Feng, have been eliminated, so today's commemoration is especially worthy of a warm celebration. Ye Dedi then delivered a speech, which was lengthy. In the afternoon, a recreational performance was held at the Minhang Public Education Center, with many programs and a very crowded audience. The performance ended at 6 p.m.

Celebrations by Various Organizations

Garrison Headquarters: The Songhu Garrison Headquarters held a Prime Minister's Birthday Commemoration at 9 a.m. yesterday. All staff members attended, with Commander Tai as the chairman. After the ceremony, the chairman delivered a speech, roughly stating that, whether during Commemoration Week or other anniversaries, we cannot simply go through the motions and consider it done. We must review the Prime Minister's personality and career to deepen our impression. My personal feeling today is that the so-called Prime Minister's revolution had its background and was needed by the times, so it was able to succeed. This statement is not entirely true. The Chinese revolution certainly had spatial and temporal backgrounds. Spatially, countries such as the Jews, Korea, and India also had this background. Temporally, after China was occupied by the Manchus, it was invaded by the great powers, and the need for revolution existed even before the Prime Minister was born. However, the Chinese revolution could only be realized and succeed with the Prime Minister. The reason why the Prime Minister was the Prime Minister was different from others. In my opinion, the reason why the Prime Minister was able to advocate revolution and succeed lies in three points: (1) a spirit of sacrifice; (2) a sense of responsibility; and (3) studying. The speech lasted two hours and adjourned at 11 a.m.

The Navy Fleet: Yesterday, the captains of the naval vessels stationed at Gaochang Temple, including Hai Rong, Chu You, Chu Qian, Chu Tai, Jiang Yuan, Jiang Zhen, Yong Sui, Lian Jing, Jing An, Yu Zhang, Gong Sheng, Yong Sheng, Yi Sheng, Hu Sun, Gan Lu, Hai Gu, etc., were ordered by Chen Shaokuan, Acting Minister of the Navy, to gather on the deck of the Hai Rong Cruiser at 8 a.m. yesterday to hold an enlarged Prime Minister's Birthday Commemoration Meeting. Several hundred officers and soldiers from various vessels attended. Chen Shaokuan chaired the meeting. After the ceremony, the Chairman reported on the significance of commemorating the Prime Minister's birthday and how the military should follow the Prime Minister's spirit of fearlessness and perseverance to fulfill the Navy's mission for the Party. The tone was passionate, and after the speech, slogans were cheered, and photos were taken. The meeting adjourned.

Dozens of personnel from the three offices attended, with Chen Xunyong, Commander of the Training Fleet, as the chairman. Cai Linbing of the Navy Special Party Headquarters reported on the significance of the commemoration. The ceremony was completed at 12 p.m., and the meeting adjourned.

Two Railways Party Headquarters: The Executive Committee of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways Special Party Headquarters held a celebration meeting yesterday morning at 10 a.m. at the Tiantong'an Station to commemorate the 65th anniversary of the Prime Minister's birth. Present were representatives from the two Railways Administration, Standing Committee members of the First District Party Headquarters, staff members of the Labor Reorganization Committee, representatives from various trade unions of the McGin Road and Wusong factories, and staff members of the committee, totaling more than 70 people. Wang Renzhou and Lian Ze then spoke successively. Finally, slogans were shouted, and the meeting adjourned.

Yesterday's Launching Ceremony of the Yixian Warship

The central government sent Xiong Shihui as a representative to give a speech, and Sun Ke's daughter performed the bottle-breaking ceremony.

The Prime Minister's alias is Yixian. The Prime Minister's birthday marks the implementation of the Prime Minister's naval plan and the continuation of construction. The Navy Department's newly built Yixian warship held a launching ceremony at the Jiangnan Shipyard in Gaochang Temple yesterday. Mr. Sun Zhe-sheng, Minister of Railways, was specially invited to have his wife break the bottle, but as Mrs. Sun was slightly indisposed, her eight-year-old daughter represented her in the bottle-breaking ceremony. Details of the program and ship construction have been reported previously. The details of yesterday's launching are summarized as follows:

Arrangement of the Rostrum: The rostrum was erected in the middle of the naval Jiangnan Shipyard, facing the Huangpu River, in a square shape. On both sides were stands for guests, each in a rectangular shape. The three platforms were arranged in a U-shape. The top of the platform was covered with a reed shed, and a layer of oil paper was sandwiched inside to prevent wind and rain. Behind the platform and on both sides of the stands were wooden ladders. At the east entrance, the national flag of green, white, and red electric lights was brightly hung, shining brightly. The sides and back of the platform were also lined with reed sheds, while the front was surrounded by railings. In the center of the platform hung the Party and national flags and a portrait of the Prime Minister. Incense was burned in front, filling the hall with fragrance. The four walls were covered with various slogans and flags made by the Naval Special Party Headquarters. The Yixian warship was displayed in front of the platform, with the bow facing the Prime Minister's portrait. A champagne bottle was hung below, wrapped in green and white ribbons and inserted with two Party and national flags. The stern faced the Huangpu River.

Details of the Launch: After the ceremony, the bottle-breaking ceremony was held by Sun Ke's daughter, Suiying. His wife, Chen Shuying, did not attend due to other matters and only sent a congratulatory message, which read: "November 12, the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, is the auspicious day of the Prime Minister's birth anniversary. The Yixian warship is completed today and will be launched for a trial run. Shuying is honored to attend the grand ceremony. I respectfully offer this message to congratulate: Science and technology advance, and its use is extensive. Railways spread on land, and aircraft fly in the sky. The vast sea, the giant ship embarks on a long journey. Holding this weapon, it travels thousands of miles. Transportation is established, and military preparedness is also managed. Heroes compete, and the waves reach the East Sea. Self-strengthening and consolidation require precision in weapons. There is a way to seek precision, and we must rise up and move forward. Learn from the masters, abandon our shortcomings, and seek illumination. We are pleased to celebrate the Prime Minister's birth on this auspicious day. The initial voyage of this ship coincides with the honored name. Breaking the bottle and testing the water, the sea surface is clear. The whole country rejoices and unifies into one. Consolidating our maritime defense is the first step. Spreading our national flag across the eight seas, the foundation of great harmony, the glory of the Chinese, I offer this eulogy to express my sincerity." Sun Ke's daughter standing at the bow, waiting for workers to remove the wooden piles from the bottom of the ship. It took about forty minutes before Miss Sun raised the champagne bottle and smashed it against the bow. The bottle broke, and champagne flowed straight down, filling the air with fragrance. At the same time, the ship slowly entered the water. The Naval Aviation Office dispatched two aircraft, Jiang Ou and Jiang Yi, at 3:30 p.m., to soar in the air and scatter small leaflets printed with colorful paper. The whole audience cheered, applauded, and thunderously applauded. Military music played in unison, and firecrackers sounded continuously. The lively scene was truly rare.

Participating Guests: Representatives from the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and the Commanders-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force were represented by Xiong Shihui, Commander of the Songhu Garrison. The Executive Yuan sent Yuan Liang, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, as a representative. Chen Shaokuan, Vice Minister of the Navy, Li Shijia, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Navy, and other naval commanders of the Second Fleet, Jiang Yuan, Chu You, Chu Qian, Chu Tai, Chu Guan, and Chu Tong, as well as ship captains and captains, and local gentry and businessmen, Yu Qiaqing, and other male and female guests, totaled more than three hundred people. Chen Shaokuan was the chairman, Shi Guoxian was the master of ceremonies, and Li Shijia, Ren Guangyu, Zheng Youyi, Ma Deji, and others were in charge of reception.

Chairman's Speech: After the ceremony, Chairman Chen Shaokuan delivered a speech, roughly stating: "Representatives from the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Commanders-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, the Executive Yuan, distinguished guests, and naval generals, today is the day of the launching ceremony of the Yixian warship. We are honored to have you all come. This Yixian warship took eight months to build. It was originally completed earlier and could have been launched earlier, but because the ship is named Yixian, we had to wait until today, the Prime Minister's birthday, to hold the launching ceremony. This is also a way to commemorate the Prime Minister. Since the unification of the north and south by the National Government, the Navy has launched three new warships, Xianning, Yong Sui, and Minquan, but the ships are smaller. The Yixian is two or three times larger than the previous ships, and all the construction is the latest (details of the ship's construction omitted). From the experience of suppressing rebellion and suppressing the Communists in recent years, and to increase our self-defense capabilities against foreign countries, it is imperative to increase naval equipment. Therefore, even in this difficult financial situation, we still insist on advocating construction. The total construction cost of this ship is more than 2.8 million yuan. Although we don't have enough funds now, we will continue to work tirelessly to find ways to complete it. We hope to complete it by the early winter or late summer and autumn of next year, so that it can serve the people and serve the Party and the country in the future. Now that the rebels have been suppressed and the financial situation of the National Government should improve, we will naturally pay attention to various constructions. Naval construction should not lag behind. There will be new warships launched in the future, and we will still invite you all to participate. The Navy is the people's armed force. We hope that all representatives and guests will give us more guidance so that we can fulfill our duties."

Representative's Speech: After the Chairman's speech, Xiong Shihui, representative of the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and the Commanders-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, gave a speech, roughly stating: "Today is the 65th anniversary of the Prime Minister's birthday and the day of the launching of the new Yixian warship. I am honored to be here on behalf of the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and the Commanders-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force. Sixty-four years ago today was the day our Prime Minister was born. The Prime Minister fought for equality and freedom for the Chinese nation. What we have today is all thanks to the Prime Minister. Yesterday was the celebration of World Peace Day. To achieve true world peace, we must first seek our own freedom and equality. The Navy is a necessary facility. The Yixian warship has a displacement of only over 1,500 tons, but in times of financial difficulty, such construction is commendable for the efforts of the Navy comrades. I hope we will follow the Prime Minister's teachings and strive for the freedom and equality of the entire Chinese nation." Yuan Liang, representative of the Executive Yuan, then delivered a speech, saying: "Today is the launching of the Yixian warship. I am here on behalf of the Executive Yuan to participate and say a few words. At a time when maritime competition is most intense, the first thing is to revitalize the Navy. The first thing to revitalize the Navy is to build warships. The Chairman just reported that Yixian is the fourth warship to be launched sixteen years later, which shows the efforts of the Navy comrades. This ship is named Yixian. Yixian is the Prime Minister's alias. The Prime Minister had a great naval plan. Today's launching ceremony may be based on the meaning of the Prime Minister's great naval plan. Then today is not only the anniversary of the successful establishment of the new Navy, but also the anniversary of the beginning of the successful realization of the Prime Minister's great naval plan." (Sun Ke's representative's speech omitted due to length)

Chairman's Reply: After the Chairman's reply, Xi Chen Shaokuan delivered a reply, saying: "Distinguished representatives, distinguished guests, distinguished workers, and distinguished generals and soldiers, today, we are very grateful for the guidance and hopes of the representatives of the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Commanders-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, and the Executive Yuan, and we are gradually ashamed. From now on, the Navy will follow your teachings and work harder to live up to your expectations. We also have 120,000 points of sincerity in hoping that you will continue to give us more guidance and more support. (Omission) Our dear workers have been working day and night, which is commendable, but we must understand that the central government is in a difficult financial situation. We cannot always ask the central government for a large amount of funds to build the Navy, so the construction cost of Yixian is still the result of the hard work and savings of all the generals and soldiers this year, as well as the consolidation of several agencies and the sale of many obsolete ships." (Omission)

Yixian Construction: Keel laid on April 10, 1919; launched on November 12, 1919; completed in March 1920; value of 2.8 million yuan; manufactured by Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy.

Convention Slogans: Long live the Kuomintang of China! Long live the Republic of China! Long live the National Government! Long live the revolutionary Navy! Long live the Yixian warship!

Public Works Bureau Decides to Ban Dog Racing Tracks Last Night

Measures Temporarily Not Announced

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Works Bureau decided to close the dog racing tracks in the Settlement after a long discussion at its meeting last night. It is also heard that the measures for the ban have been decided, but they are unwilling to announce them for the time being. The anti-gambling movement in the Settlement was launched on August 8th. On that day, Fessenden, Director-General of the Public Works Bureau, sent a letter to Qu Laide, Chief of the Police of the Public Works Bureau, stating that the commercialized gambling in Shanghai was more extensive than in most cities of comparable size. Although dog racing tracks, horse racing tracks, and jai alai are not strictly protected, they are allowed to be established, and the gains and losses are enormous. The Chinese all say that such gambling is directly related to armed robbery, kidnapping, and theft. It is believed that such gambling does indeed have an impact on crime in Shanghai. The sending of this letter was the prelude to the anti-gambling campaign in the Settlement. Later, Chief of Police Qu Laide replied to Director-General Fessenden on August 22nd, denouncing the evils of gambling, saying that gambling is directly related to crime, and that wherever there are large-scale gambling dens, there will inevitably be many crimes. He also said that the scope of gambling in Shanghai is far greater than elsewhere, so unless this worst kind of harm is eradicated, such as illegal opium trade, gambling, and places of general promiscuity, crime in Shanghai will continue to increase. Therefore, he advocated exerting all the power of his office to ban all kinds of commercial or other gambling. As a result, the Settlement authorities actively carried out the anti-gambling movement, and banning dog racing tracks was a matter of utmost urgency. British Consul-General Brenan, Director-General of the Public Works Bureau Fessenden, and Chief of Police Qu Laide also met on the 3rd of this month to discuss not only banning dog racing tracks in the Settlement, but also completely prohibiting them. The Police Committee of the Public Works Bureau also agreed on the prohibition method on the 6th of this month and submitted it to the Board of Directors. The Board of Directors of the Public Works Bureau held a meeting in the Director-General's office at 4:30 PM yesterday to discuss the matter until 7:40 PM, focusing on the issue of banning dog racing for three hours. Fessenden excused himself in advance. Regarding the content of the meeting, he said that the Board of Directors had made a special resolution not to announce a single word. However, according to reliable sources, this newspaper's reporter learned that the Board of Directors of the Public Works Bureau did indeed decide to ban dog racing last night. As for the date of implementation and the measures for the ban, the Public Works Bureau authorities are unwilling to announce them for the time being. It is faintly heard that the Public Works Bureau will notify the promoters of the dog racing tracks to stop dog racing gambling within a reasonable time limit. If they still do not comply after the deadline, the Public Works Bureau will take severe measures when necessary, such as withdrawing police protection, prohibiting traffic, and suing its operators and spectators.

Closing Accounts and Collecting Debts Difficult to Separate

Since there is no way to decide on a business policy, how can one advance or retreat? The issue of hiring employees for the year-end closing of accounts, which is attracting social attention, has now been decided by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. It is proposed to change the general closing date to the day before the beginning of spring each year and submit it to the Bureau of Social Affairs for forwarding to the government for approval and filing. However, it is not yet certain whether the government will approve the request. Some time ago, Mr. Wang Yansong, a standing committee member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, reported on the progress of the Industrial and Commercial Conference at the Chamber of Commerce and mentioned the opinion of Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, who believed that closing accounts and collecting debts could be regarded as two separate issues. Year-end closing of accounts is fine, and collecting debts can be done at the convenience of the merchant, until the end of January or the end of February, without violating government orders or commercial conditions. It seems that this matter will be implemented by order of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. However, whether closing accounts and collecting debts can be separated into two is a matter of great importance to the business community. According to Yan E-sheng, secretary of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, his opinion is as follows: Although the old practice of closing accounts in our country's business community is divided into three periods, the relationship between the Dragon Boat Festival and the Mid-Autumn Festival is still light. The most important thing is the year-end. As the saying goes, "Take a look at the Dragon Boat Festival, and pay back half at the Mid-Autumn Festival." By the end of the year, it must be cleared. This is why there is the term "year-end." However, the key to the year-end closing of accounts in stores is not in the internal "closing" but in the external "collecting." It must be that the closing after the debt collection is clear is the true closing. If the year-end is only closing but not collecting, two difficulties will inevitably occur in practice: First, after the year-end debt collection is completed, the shareholders can decide on the actual operating results of the current year and decide whether to expand, continue, or stop the business. If the year-end is only closing but not collecting, the shareholders can see a certain amount of profit in the ledger, but in fact, it is unknown whether there will be bad debts or bad debts or 20% or 30% discounts when collecting this account. Then, the business policy for the coming year will inevitably be impossible to decide. For example, Qian Zhong, the leader of all industries, closes accounts at the end of the year, but the collection of debts must be done by the end of January or the end of February. Then, how to operate during the period after the closing of accounts and before the collection of debts is a major issue that can be studied. Second, stores mostly dismiss or hire after the closing of accounts. On the employer's side, it can be decided to increase or decrease the number of employees based on the business policy for the coming year. On the employee's side, after the year-end handling of accounts is completed, whether it is dismissal or career change, the procedures can be handled clearly. If only the closing of accounts can be done but not the collection of debts at the end of the year, on the one hand, it is impossible to determine the increase or decrease of employees based on the overall business situation. On the other hand, if an employee is to be dismissed, if it is done at the time of the year-end closing of accounts, the accounts he has handled have not yet been collected. If the dismissal is done after the debt collection, the year-end has passed and it is not the time to do a closing. In short, the most important thing for the business community is that there must be a definite date for a practical closing every year. If the year-end can only close the internal accounts but cannot collect the external accounts, and can only "close" but not "bind," it will inevitably feel greatly inconvenient in business and will never be passable. The government should pay attention to this level.

Both Sides Hire Westerners as Witnesses to Question Witnesses, Touching on Trivial Matters, Lawyer Requests Cause Judge Dissatisfaction, Judge Orders Trial by Panel

The case of economic doctor Tang Huixuan suing his wife, Zou Aizhen, and Chen Genwei for adultery, dissatisfied with the first-instance judgment of the Criminal Court of the Shanghai Local Court declaring Zou and Chen not guilty, appealed to the collegial panel of the original court. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Judge Qian Chengjun continued to open the investigation court to interrogate the facts. More than 400 people crowded the hearing. Chen Genwei lives in the back building, and my daughter and I live in the front building. Q: Did your second daughter and Chen Genwei go out? A: Because there are children in the family, they can't leave. Sometimes when the children are sick, several people go out together. Q: Did they commit adultery? A: No, how could I let them commit adultery if I lived together? He came to arrest people, and Chen Genwei was still sick. Aizhen went out to ask what was going on, and they twisted Aizhen away. Q: Is Chen Genwei good? A: Not frivolous. If he were frivolous, I wouldn't want to keep such a person at home. Q: How do you and your daughter sleep? A: Because it was hot, my second daughter and I slept on a mat on the floor, and the third daughter slept on a large mat. The big child slept on the bed. Q: The front and back buildings are very close? A: Although they are close, how can they be so disciplined? Q: Then why did Tang Huixuan say that your daughter committed adultery? A: Because he wanted to facilitate a divorce. The official asked

Russian Fails to Pay Wages, Relies on Force, and Shoots People

Almost Inciting a Major Uproar, Russian Driver Still Dares to Lie

The Central Research Institute on Route Tenant de la Tour, Shanghai, is currently constructing a large-scale Western-style building. This project was contracted by a Russian named Lei, who then subcontracted it to another Russian, JOHN GOLDSTEIN, as the second-level contractor. This Russian then subcontracted it to a Chinese named Zhang Chongwei as the third-level contractor. All workers were hired by Zhang. Construction has been underway for several months and is nearing completion. The day before yesterday afternoon, a large group of workers demanded wages from Zhang. Zhang replied that the Russian had not yet paid. The workers then went to inquire with Lei, the first-level Russian contractor, who claimed to have already paid the second-level Russian contractor. The workers were extremely angry that the Russian had intentionally not paid. At around 5 p.m., the second-level Russian, accompanied by three other Russians, arrived in a car. The workers immediately demanded their wages from the Russian. Unexpectedly, the Russian and the three Russians who came with him each drew handguns. The workers, fearing an incident, did not argue. Zhang Chongwei, the third-level Chinese contractor, then went to the Sixth District Police Station to report the incident (at which time the Russian had already left) and file a report. Yesterday morning at 9:10 a.m., the third-level Russian returned to the site in a car. The workers again demanded their wages and surged forward. Unexpectedly, the Russian suddenly pulled a handgun from his pocket and struck the cook of the institute, Wang Asi, on the head, causing him to bleed profusely. The handgun was seized by the workers. The workers immediately hired a car, dragged the Russian into the car, and, along with Wang Asi, the accountant Cao Deming, and two workers, took them all to the Sixth District Police Station to request an investigation. The Russian driver of the car, seeing that the Russian had been taken to the Sixth District, immediately ran to the Jing'an Temple Police Station to falsely report that the Russian had been abducted to the Sixth District. The police chief, upon receiving the report, immediately went to the Sixth District to request that the Russian be brought to him for questioning. The district chief had already interrogated him and, because the Russian's Russian-made five-shot handgun was unlicensed and he had used live ammunition to beat and injure someone, refused to release him to the police chief. He then prepared a document and sent the Russian, the injured Wang Asi, the accountant Cao Deming, two workers, and the handgun to the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Appeal in the Xintong Foreign Firm Debt Case Remanded for Retrial

Whether the Comprador's Fundraising Shareholders are Liable Depends on the Date of Withdrawal and Borrowing. The Supreme Court Remands the Case to the High Court Branch for Further Trial Based on the Above Two Points.

Guo Buqin, Zhu Yingwei, and Cao Shaochen jointly established the Xintong Foreign Firm in the 14th year of the Republic, agreeing to a capital of 20,000 taels of silver, divided into ten shares, with Guo and Zhu each subscribing three shares and Cao subscribing four shares. During operations up to August of the following year, Cao's four shares were transferred to Zhu Yingwei with Huang Jinshen acting as intermediary. At that time, no public announcement was made, so the transfer of his shares was initially unknown to outsiders. Later, the foreign firm went bankrupt, owing 18,499 taels, 1 mace, 2 candareens, and 7 cash to three money houses, Taichang, Jichang, and Xinkang Changji. Because the three money houses were unaware of the share merger, they sued Guo, Zhu, and Cao in the former Provisional Court, requesting a joint order for repayment. At the conclusion of the trial, the plaintiff's request was granted. Zhu Yingwei, one of the defendants, was responsible for the debts borrowed by him, so had no objection to the judgement. Cao Shaochen stated that since his shares had already been transferred to Zhu, he was not obligated to bear any of the firm's debts. Guo Buqin also stated that the debts owed to the three money houses had been borrowed by Zhu and should be borne by Zhu alone, so there was no involvement for him. Based on these reasons, they hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Fan Gang to appeal to the former Upper Court. On April 18th of the year before last, the court ruled to revoke the original ruling regarding the order for Cao Shaochen to repay the debt according to his shares. Cao Shaochen was not responsible for repayment of debts for money houses Taichang. The appeal of Guo Buqin was dismissed as unreasonable. After receiving the judgment, Taichang expressed dissatisfaction with the second instance court's recognition that Cao Shaochen did not need to be held responsible for repaying the debt according to his shares, and wanted to appeal to the third instance. At that time, the three-instance system for lawsuits in the concession had not yet been implemented, so the matter remained unresolved. After the authorities reached an agreement with foreign groups on the trial level system, the three money houses hired lawyers Shen Yuesheng and Zhang Deqin to appeal to the Nanjing Supreme Court regarding Cao Shaochen's part, requesting that the respondent be ordered to bear his shares as in the first instance judgment. Under the examination of court president Li You, the situation in this case should be considered under: (1) Whether the firm's shareholders are naturally responsible for debts borrowed by the comprador Zhu Yingwei. (2) If the firm's shareholders should naturally be responsible, whether the appellant had withdrawn before borrowing the debt, and if the withdrawal was after the debt, whether the creditor had agreed with the transfer of debt. The original judgment has already concluded that Zhu Yingwei can certainly represent the Xintong Foreign Firm, borrowing debts, but for point two, there was no need to examine the tickets held by the involved parties, such as ledger accounts, etc, and examine whether borrowing was before or after August 15th of the Lunar calender, that Cao had transferred his stock to Zhu. The High Court said this was incorrect and had a reason for remanding for retrial, if the appellant's stock withdrawal was before the debt borrowing, should the creditor, Taichang, been consulted according to transfer debt regulation. Based on the above reasons, the judgement remanded the case to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court for retrial. The High Court branch then notified lawyer Shen Yuesheng and Cao Shaochen, the resident of Yuanfeng Silk Factory in Furun Lane, Beijing Road, to attend the court. Court Director Hu, together with Judges Ye and Li, opened the court to re-examine the points instructed by the higher court. Because further investigation was still needed, the court announced that it would be adjourned to a later date for further hearing.

Failure to Deliver Rubber on Time, Seeking Compensation of Over 40,000 Gold

Defendant Raises the Issue of Subject of Litigation; the Company Should be Sued, Not the Individual

Li Guohua, the owner of Zhenhua Garden from Guangdong province, bought ten tons of rubber from Wu Rongchang of Xinji Company on Hankou Road. Li was in need of this material for manufacturing products, and they agreed on a price of 405 taels of silver per ton. They signed a contract for delivery in the months of May, June, and July. A deposit of 400 yuan was paid. However, Wu failed to deliver the goods on time. Li then had to purchase from other sources, and the price was surprisingly high. The ten tons of rubber cost him over 50,400 yuan. If Wu had not broken the contract, the cost would have been only 5,670 yuan. Now, he has suffered a loss of 44,730 yuan. In addition, the wages and food for the workers hired during May, June, and July also cost 4,023 yuan. Both of these amounts should be compensated by Wu. He appealed to Wu for resolution, but Wu ignored him. Li then hired a lawyer and sued in the Special District Local Court. The defendant was summoned yesterday and hired lawyers Shen Yuesheng and Zhang Deqin to appear in court, raising the issue of the subject of litigation. According to lawyer Shen, Wu Rongchang is the manager of Xinji Limited Company, which is a British company. This transaction was made by Wu on behalf of the company, not as an individual act. If there is a dispute, the plaintiff should negotiate with the company. It is inappropriate for the plaintiff to sue Li personally, and the court should first make an intermediate ruling. The plaintiff's lawyer also made a defense. The court official did not proceed with the case due to this issue and adjourned the session for further review.

An Old Monk Kneels to Die

Kowtows to Tram Driver, Hoping to be Run Over by the Tram

Tram number 213 of the Public Concession Tram Company, running from Yangshupu to Lujiiawan in the French Concession, was traveling south to north on the Bund at around 11:30 a.m. yesterday. As the tram approached the intersection of Beijing Road, the driver suddenly saw an old monk, about forty years old, with ragged clothes and a slight beard, kneeling in the middle of the track about ten feet away, facing the tram. The driver immediately braked upon seeing the monk kneeling in front. Unexpectedly, the monk kowtowed several times to the driver, saying, "Thank you, I am very grateful. Please hurry and run me over to kill me!" The driver was shocked and, fearing that he was mentally ill, immediately got out of the tram to check. A pedestrian also saw this and came forward to help the monk up, asking him why he was doing this. The monk remained silent, seeming to have a sorrowful secret that could not be told. Upon closer inspection, he did not appear to be mentally ill. The monk then walked aimlessly along the Bund, and the tram drove away. Later, fearing that he would throw himself into the river, the workers drove the monk to the back road. The audience was shocked.

Large Quantities of Narcotics Found in Italian Ship

190 Pounds of Heroin, Worth Over 250,000 Yuan

According to the Shanghai Times, yesterday (11th), customs officers discovered 190 pounds of heroin, worth over 250,000 yuan, in the cargo unloaded from the Italian ship "Dilauna." If sold in the interior, the price would be doubled. This can truly be said to be one of the largest batches of imported narcotics seized in recent years. The ship arrived on Friday and docked at the Gonghexing Wharf. Customs had received prior information that a large quantity of narcotics had been secretly transported from Constantinople on the ship and instructed the inspectors to pay special attention to the ship's cargo. After thoroughly inspecting most of the cargo from Constantinople, they came across several boxes of candied fruit. Upon opening them, they found that each box of candied fruit contained several small packages of high-grade heroin. The packaging and labeling were completely identical to the candied fruit packaging, making it difficult to detect without close inspection. Therefore, all 36 boxes with the "candied fruit" label were transported to the customs examination room for detailed inspection. A total of 190 pounds were discovered. However, it is believed that this seizure is only a small portion of the narcotics smuggled from various ports in the Near East to Shanghai. The bill of lading for this candied fruit did not indicate the name or shop number of the consignee. No one went to customs to pay taxes and pick up the goods at the time. The insurer was not labeled on the packaging and transportation, so it is difficult to investigate the owner of the goods. It is also heard that the Hong Kong Customs was the first to receive the information.

Bean Curd Ah Chang Chopped with Six Axes

White-collar worker was murdered by others, seriously injured and life-threatening

The local white-collar worker nicknamed Bean Curd Ah Chang, aged 32, lives in Bailinan Road in western Shanghai. He used to work in a bean curd factory, but had been unemployed for many years. After becoming a follower of a certain leader, he became an associate of white-collar workers. In the area, he had a slight reputation. At about 5:30 a.m. the day before yesterday, Ah Chang left home and went to a small stove shop near the area (that is, in the middle of Bailinan Road) to drink tea. He had just sat down and was washing his face when a car suddenly drove to the entrance of the stove shop. The engine stopped and four strong men in long clothes jumped out of the car. One held a handgun and two others each held a sharp axe. One person walked into the stove shop and dragged Ah Chang out with all his might. Three people then rushed forward. One pressed the handgun against Ah Chang's head, threatening to shoot. The other two raised their sharp axes and chopped violently. Ah Chang immediately cried out in pain and fell to the ground, covered in blood. He was struck with an axe in the arm, hand, and shoulder. His buttocks and legs were also struck with three axes. He sustained a total of six injuries. Seeing that their goal had been achieved, the murderers immediately got into the car and drove away. At that time, there were few people in the area. Only one or two people saw it, but they did not dare to speak out because the murderers were armed. Later, when his family found out, they immediately hired a car to take him to the Red Cross Hospital on Haigen Road for treatment. He was seriously injured and his life was in danger. It is said that all the murderers were known to Ah Chang (also white-collar workers). Because of helping others in the same group, they had accumulated deep grudges, so they seized the opportunity to avenge their old enemies and committed this heinous act.

The Lawsuit Over the Zhou Miaogen Brothers' Inheritance

(10) Qianjiazhai land, eight points (price 800 yuan). (11) Xijiabang west land, one and a half mu (price 6,000 taels per mu). (12) Qinjianong land, one mu (price over 4,000 taels). (13) Wangjia Ancestral Hall front land, seven and a half mu, rear land, three and a half mu (price 11,000 taels). (14)

Jiu Tu land, 15 mu (price 15,000 yuan). (15) Baoshan County Yinhang Factory, Yanghang Factory, Jiangwan Factory, three pieces of land, about 20 mu (price 500 yuan per mu). Except for the first property, which was inhabited by the plaintiff, the rest were managed by the grandfather Zhiliang, and the income was divided equally between the two wives. Later, the father Bingzhi and the biological mother Zhou died. The funeral arrangements were all handled by the plaintiff and others in the name of the eldest wife. However, the defendant did not follow the intentions of the grandfather. The second to fifteenth properties were all managed by the defendant. After negotiation, the defendant insisted on being unreasonable and refused to agree. The defendant sold the fourth property without authorization and did not divide the proceeds equally. If he is allowed to manage it without urging, the property will be swallowed up. How can the legal rights of the plaintiff be guaranteed? Now the plaintiff is unemployed at home and has no food or clothing, so he has no choice but to file a lawsuit for relief, requesting the court to order the defendant to divide the property equally. The case was heard yesterday morning by Judge He Ji. The defendant did not attend. Judge He questioned the plaintiff and announced that the hearing would be adjourned to a later date for further investigation.

Jingwei Yarn Factory Suffers Carelessness Yesterday

At about 4:30 p.m. yesterday, a cotton-making machine in the machine room of the Jingwei Yarn Factory at No. 31, Yuezhou Road, Gongping Road, Hongkou, suddenly caught fire. The flames soared and sparks flew everywhere. In an instant, a large amount of cotton was burned and several machines were damaged. The Yangshupu Fire Brigade drove to the scene to put out the fire. It took some time to extinguish the fire. It is estimated that the loss is about several thousand yuan.

Murder Case of Kicking the Waist

The deceased had a stomach prone to rupture; the suspect is detained pending a scheduled sentencing.

Wang Linxiang, a laborer from Jiangbei working on the road, had an altercation with Dong Hongjin, a laborer from Yong (Ningbo), over a debt of four small silver coins at noon on the 3rd of this month at the target range in northern Sichuan. Inadvertently, Wang kicked Dong in the left waist, causing him to fall to the ground. Dong immediately vomited the food he had eaten and died. Hua Sheng, a Western detective from the Tihua Road Police Station, arrested Wang and brought him to the Special District Court for interrogation. The details were reported in this newspaper the day before yesterday. Judge Ge Zhitian continued the trial in court. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, stated the case and said that the police were prosecuting under Article 296 of the Criminal Law for injury causing death. According to the forensic examination, the deceased's stomach was three times larger than normal, making it prone to rupture upon impact. Wu Lifu, a fellow worker, testified that the defendant kicked the deceased in the waist three times, causing him to fall, vomit food, and become unable to speak. Although there was no loud argument between the two sides, the kick was not playful. The two had already argued at 8:00 AM that morning. Zhou Wanggui, another worker, testified that he had invited the deceased to work. He saw the defendant kick the deceased in the waist once, and he immediately shouted to stop him, but the defendant kicked him again. The deceased then fell to the ground without speaking and died after a while. Dong A'tu, the deceased's cousin, reported that the deceased had no previous illnesses and that his aunt was still in Yong (Ningbo) and had not yet come to Shanghai, requesting that the defendant be severely punished. The defendant insisted that he did not intentionally kill the deceased and asked for leniency. Judge Ge, after reviewing the evidence, appointed a lawyer to defend the defendant and ordered Wang Linxiang to be detained pending a scheduled sentencing.

Tianqingxiang Fur Store on Henan Road near the Polo Ground is selling various types of fur goods at discounted prices. Mr. Xu is very experienced with fur, and the goods he selects are not only of excellent quality but also purchased at low prices. Regular customers of the store have always been very satisfied and have praised it highly. This year, the store's fur goods are even cheaper than last year because the lease on the premises is expiring and they are eager to sell off their inventory. It is reported that the store has already started a major clearance sale from today, disregarding any losses, with discounts as high as 10% or 20% off the original price.

Daputong Fellow Countrymen Discuss Relocation of Public Cemetery

For the purpose of providing repose to fellow countrymen of the Guangdong Dapu County residing in Shanghai, the gentry and merchants have established a public cemetery on Lujiabang Road for over a century. Recently, due to the road widening and the construction of municipal buildings, the public cemetery is obstructing the view and it is proposed to relocate it. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, leaders from all walks of life in Shanghai were convened at the Dapu Fellow Countrymen Association to discuss the implementation plan. Over 130 people attended, and Yang Shoushan was elected as chairman. The reasons for relocating the public cemetery and the subsequent arrangements were reported. It was resolved to purchase another piece of land and rebuild the cemetery. A general meeting of all Dapu fellow countrymen in Shanghai will be held at Hengshan Hall on Sanguantang Road at 11:00 AM on Thursday, the 20th of this month (the first day of the tenth month), to discuss all preparatory methods and to elect new directors of Hengshan Hall and members of the cemetery construction preparatory committee.
